Free Talk

Hunger in Tang Poetry 218

— Zepu

After the An Lushan Rebellion, Tang society fell into a dim state of turmoil and instability. Political turmoil was to be expected, but the economic exhaustion was more severe than one could imagine. Because in that kind of situation ("Under heaven, all countries turn to ten thousand cities, but there is no city without armor and weapons.") and ("Of the two hundred prefectures in Shandong of the Han Dynasty, a thousand villages and ten thousand trees grow thorny shrubs."), the collapse of the economic foundation was a necessary result. The people who lived at that time tasted some suffering, but imagined events are not reliable, and it is only the handwriting in historical records that can give us an accurate explanation.

In Tang poetry, much of the social conditions of that time is preserved, especially in the works of Du Fu and Bai Juyi, which contain more descriptions of this kind of actual social phenomena. I have always enjoyed reading Tang poetry, and I pay special attention to these kinds of works; among them, what I cannot forget the most is the misery of the people who suffered from (hunger) at that time.

Among the common people, whose desires are not high and whose thoughts are simple, (having food) and (not having food) really determined all the joy and suffering of their lives; moreover, it is only the two questions of (having food) and (not having food) that are the main factors that determine the prosperity of any nation's history. Before the An Lushan Rebellion, Tang society was a happy society of peace and prosperity. At that time, politics was clear and the economy was abundant, and the lives of the people were very comfortable and smooth; but since the Sound of Rainbow Feathers and Robes by Emperor Xuanzong was startled by the drums of Yuyang, the Central Plains fell into the sorrow of famine and turmoil. Du Fu has a poem "Recalling the Past," which describes the two different situations before and after that time quite thoroughly. The poem says:

(Recalling the prosperous days of the Kaiyuan era, even small towns stored houses with families. Rice flowed like grease, millet was white, and the public and private granaries were full and substantial. There were no wolves or tigers on the roads of the Nine Provinces, and traveling far did not require choosing an auspicious day. Fine silk and Lu silk were everywhere, men plowed and women weaved without neglecting their duties. The sage in the palace played the Cloud Gate music, and all friends under heaven were like close relatives. For more than a hundred years, there were no disasters, and the rites of Shusun and the laws of Xiao He prevailed. Who would have heard that a single piece of silk was worth ten thousand coins? Today, plowing the fields to plant grain causes bloodshed. The palaces in Luoyang have been burned and destroyed, and the ancestral temples have become dens for foxes and rabbits. I am heartbroken and cannot bear to ask the elders, for fear of hearing about the chaos and separation from the beginning!...)

Old Du was a person who personally experienced both the era of peace and the era of rebellion, so what he recorded was true. From this, we can see that the situation changed completely.

Since the era before the An Lushan Rebellion was an era of peace and prosperity, the people's livelihood was naturally happy. This is also clearly visible in the early Tang poetry. The reason why the collections of Li Bai, Cen Shen, Gao Shi, Wang Wei, and others are full of the (smell of wine) is because they were in a comfortable environment; but in the later Tang poetry, it is full of the glaring words of hunger and cold. Look:

(I want to go to face hunger and thirst with you, ...... my youngest son has already died of hunger!) (Expressing My Feelings on the Way to Fengxian County)

(Autumn comes and turns to hunger and cold.) (Because of Imperial Censor Cui Wu and Pengzhou Gao)

(Hunger causes people to exchange children to eat.) (Farewell to Tang Fifteen Commandments)

(The faces of hungry young children are always sad!) (Madman)

(On this day, hunger and cold drive me to the roadside.) (Do Not Suspect Each Other)

(Hunger and cold press toward the corner.) (Leaving Jiangling Nampu by Boat)

(A woman with no food and no children.) (Presenting to Wu Lang Again)

(My foolish daughter bites me because of hunger.) (Peng Ya Trip)

(I endure hunger all day long, going west and then east.) (White Egret Trip)

(Enduring hunger on Floating Cloud Cliff.) (Eight Elegies)

(Picking oak acorns in the stream due to hunger.) (Eight Elegies)

(Hunger and cold eternally look at each other.) (Remnant Joy One)

(Hunger and cold chirp all day long.) (Phoenix Terrace)

The above are from Du Fu.

(In a year of hunger, there are no leftover grains, ... suffering from hunger disfigures the face.) (Expressing Sentiments)

(Singing for hunger and snow four times.) (Singing for Hunger and Snow)

(A hungry person values a single meal.) (Autumn Thoughts Eleven)

(The heart is about to collapse from late hunger!) (Autumn Thoughts Seventeen)

(Eating unnamed vegetables due to hunger.) (Living in Qing'an)

(Hungry children and hungry horses sweep flowers to feed.) (Cold Food Day in Jiyuan Three)

(Starving to death, embracing empty mountains.) (Mourning Lu Yin)

The above are from Meng Dongye.

(The lanes and wells are full of people who have died of hunger.) (Returning to Pengcheng)

(Hungry cries are but chirps.) (Obstructed by Wind on Dongting Lake, Giving to Zhang Eleven Shu)

The above are from Han Changli.

(Picking these to fill the hungry intestines.) (Watching Wheat Harvesting)

(Saving these to relieve the bitter hunger.) (Gathering Rehmannia)

(Guarding poverty and hunger all year round.) (There Is a Tomb in the Hill)

(What to do when hunger comes?) (Continuing Ancient Poems Three)

(The heat is fierce, the days are long, and hunger makes me want to die!) (Catching Locusts)

(Dining and drinking causes hunger and thirst.) (Tying Up Rong People)

The above are from Bai Juyi. In addition, Yuan Jie's (Morning meals are grass roots, evening meals are still tree bark.) ("Spring Mausoleum Trip") is also nothing more than writing about the misery of hunger!

For the common people who lived in troubled times, suffering from hunger and cold was not considered a strange thing. The suffering of the Chinese people after the middle of the eighth century was like this, and the suffering in later troubled times was also like this. When I read Du Fu's sentence (Hunger causes people to exchange children to eat), I could not help but think of the events of people exchanging children to eat during the famine in various provinces of Gansu and Shaanxi in past years! As for eating flowers, eating grass roots, and eating tree bark, that is even more commonly seen and heard in ancient and modern times, but eating stone powder, eating sand, and eating soil was unprecedented in the past!

As the saying goes: (I would rather be a dog in times of peace than a commoner in times of chaos), this saying is really true. Dogs in peaceful times are indeed much happier than people in turbulent times. Because the dogs in peaceful times have things to eat and places to play, while the common people in turbulent times not only have to suffer from hunger and cold, but also do not have freedom of movement!

Donkey Cart 219

— Yao Yiyun

丨A Sketch from the Outskirts of Xi'an丨

Dust, stirred up by the clumsy wheels of a rolling cart, flies up and billows like surging angry waves.

A middle-aged man sits leisurely in the donkey cart. The cart's decorations, somewhat like a cabin on a Jiangnan boat, display a national essence-style beauty, with orange tassels hanging from the window edges.

His eyes don't glance at the crows and eagles soaring in the sky; he only peers through ancient, wide-rimmed, white copper spectacles perched on the tip of his nose, focusing on a scroll of a book held in his hand, reading line by line. I cannot know what national essence masterpiece it is; I imagine it's probably "Shi Gong An" or "Seven Heroes and Five Gallants." His dedication is enough to make me deeply admire him; this kind of diligent spirit is enough to allow Chinese culture to catch up with the world's trends head-on. Furthermore, his serene and leisurely attitude fully reveals the ancient style of our vast nation of five thousand years. Look at him, calmly reading his book while holding the rope whip, with a loud but feeble crack hitting the ground, whereupon the donkey once again stirs up its flagging spirit and moves forward more quickly. Thus, another burst of dust flies up and billows like surging angry waves.

The wheels always seem too clumsy, and their movement is extremely slow. Their rumbling turning humorously symbolizes the advancement of Northwest culture.

The Exile 220

— Hei Ying

A friend told me a story about an exile, which I thought was worth writing down丨丨丨

(After being exiled to the desolate island of Riku, my young, dark-faced friend 丨丨丨丨 Sumaleng and I lived in two completely different worlds, and we haven't heard from each other since.

(But, you know: I can't forget him.

(In the winter of 1930, I was unemployed in Shanghai, living a very miserable life for some time. After receiving an invitation from a Dutch ×× newspaper, I immediately went there and started my life as a journalist. On my first day at work, someone warned me: this is an imperialist colony, and freedom of speech is very restricted. I already had a fairly clear understanding of the faces of imperialists; however, it was more than two months after living in this temple that I was directly threatened and imprisoned for a piece of writing.

(A month in prison was really hard to get through! By chance, I met Sumaleng here. 丨丨丨 At that time, he was the editor-in-chief of a Malay newspaper and had also gotten into trouble because of his writing. If it weren't for him, just dealing with the prison guards would have been enough to annoy me to death. Because at that time, I couldn't speak a word of Malay. Fortunately, Sumaleng was able to do a lot of work for me; moreover, his English was more fluent than mine, and his attitude was so humble, so we became good friends in less than two days.

(He once told me this:

(丨丨This is my second time in jail.

(丨丨丨Oh... how long?

(I asked, throwing away the half-inch long cigarette butt. Sumaleng stretched out his slightly rough, dark fingers and smiled bitterly at me. I asked him how many days he had left, and he replied:

(丨Almost full, just over two months left.

(Naturally, I quickly left prison and returned to the newspaper office alone. By the time Sumaleng came out, the Anti-Japanese War in Shanghai was becoming more and more intense, and it was also shaking up the rulers in the South Seas! Our freedom of speech was restricted, and our telegrams were strictly censored! But Sumaleng's newspaper bravely exposed the brutal face of Japanese imperialism! When he saw me, he always shouted:

(丨丨丨Roar, China!

(Touched by his enthusiasm, I often felt ashamed of my cowardice as a Chinese. When he was happy, he also frankly said to me:

(丨丨丨Friend, I can tell you, I have a great mission on my shoulders. What are you afraid of! Shouldn't young people be braver? Hearing about your heroic resistance, I will be even more excited. You can also see the situation of our oppression, right? You are also on our side, right? We should join hands!

(He spoke so earnestly and forcefully. As a fighter for the liberation of the weak and oppressed, Sumaleng is worthy of admiration...

(However, not long after, I heard that he had been arrested again. 丨丨This is the third time, and the situation is even more serious; the newspapers only mentioned it lightly. I went to the political department (where Sumaleng was being held) several times to see him, but I was not allowed. I returned with disappointment and indignation, clenching my teeth; but what could I do?

(A month later, without letting me see him again, Sumaleng was taken to the customs wharf and decided to be exiled to the remote and desolate island of Riku.

(Not long after, I resigned. I left ×× without any reluctance. I can't forget the young fighter who was exiled to the isolated island. ...)

I believe that even in colonies, under the strong pressure of warships, armored vehicles, airplanes, and bombs, there are clear-headed people who are active. I sympathize with those poor, exploited people. For more than ten years, I have watched how the rulers use soft and hard tactics on millions of people. Now, I have written down the story of my friend, 丨丨This is a story that is not yet finished. Sumaleng's future is long. Who dares to say that it is over just because he was exiled to a deserted island?

Mr. Village Head (10) (2) 221

— Wang Renshu

(Hmph! Two months.) Kaiyang Hemp Skin doesn't believe it. (The situation outside is unstable, there are wars everywhere; the people outside are almost wiped out, and now they want us to go and fight. The notice says two months, will they really let us back in two months? Isn't that just a fart, you won't be able to find it anywhere in a while.)

(Joke, joke.) Winterlife Cripple turned around this time and sat on the wooden strip under the notice, resting his left foot on his right foot and shaking it continuously. (What kind of work is there to do outside? Opening a public stove requires capital, being a waiter requires a security deposit. Factory work is unbearable. Yunsheng Crooked Mouth worked in a cotton mill for three years, vomited blood, and returned to his hometown. Isn't Sister-in-law Ajin's son Xiaolin beaten on his skin until he can't even bring his bones back home丨丨What kind of work is there to do outside? And, and Sheng Tu's son, crushed to death by a car on the main road! Country folks, stupid and clumsy, also want to go to Shanghai... Joke, joke!)

(You always say the same thing.) Mu Ren Lao shook his unfractured right leg. (Since ancient times, boatmen help boatmen, water helps water. When you eat the government's food, you always speak the government's words. You always want all seventy-two draftees, not leaving a single one, one by one falling into your trap.)

(Big Foot Crazy is crazy himself. He's really a mad dog, how can he bite me?) Winterlife Cripple and Mu Ren Big Foot Crazy sit facing each other, their words are on point, and even their disabilities are equal. (You're not a draftee, and I'm not a draftee, who cares about an egg. But since the superiors have said it, they have to do it.)

Dao Gou couldn't think of anything to say. He stood there blankly, watching, although he felt strange and depressed.

Big Lai Ge works as a sailor on a boat. Didn't they take the boat away that year because they wanted to recruit soldiers, and they insisted on taking Big Lai Ge? They sent them to the fiery place. When there's a war, if you don't become a soldier, you'll die; if you become a soldier, you'll also die. Mu Ren Lao closed his eyes and thought for a while, feeling that A Zhao's words made some sense. Times are chaotic, and the lives of people in the countryside are not peaceful either. Little Western Heaven 222

— By Zhang Henshui

Chapter 1: The Merchant Returns from the Road to the People, Saying Farewell to Yongshou; A Heavenly Being Arrives in Chang'an

It's not far to Little Western Heaven, there's a restaurant right there. They still used the old method: entering the shop, it's the kitchen, and only after passing through this kitchen do you reach the dining area. Under a large awning, there were ten or so tables, but it was clean. The two sat down, and Li Shilian said: I don't eat greasy things much, find something light to eat. Jia Duocai laughed: Let me state first that when eating dishes here, don't mention fish or duck, only duck and pork, which are very light, probably not even available. Li Shilian scratched his head and said: Then, you take care of ordering, I won't interfere. Jia Duocai was not polite and ordered the dishes himself. The shop assistant brought the wine pot, teacups, and chopsticks. Jia Duocai poured tea into the cup and laughed: Drinking this tea makes people not want to make a living in the Northwest. Li Shilian took the teacup and asked: Why is that? As he spoke, he picked up the cup and took a sip, smacking his lips a few times, and said: Is this water bad? I can't taste anything wrong with it. As he spoke, he picked it up and took another sip. Jia Duocai said: This water is the best water, there's nothing strange about it here, you don't need to taste it. How would you know? There are a total of 120,000 people in Xi'an city, all drinking water from a well inside the West Gate, carried in small buckets and pushed in small carts to deliver to users. It's fine if the distance is short, but if it's far, each bucket costs two or three dimes. Li Shilian said: Is there only this one well in the whole city? Jia Duocai said: Although there are wells, the water that comes out is muddy soup, not only can't you drink it, but you have to clarify it before you can wash clothes. We Southerners have water everywhere we go, but coming to this Northwest where water is used as treasure, it's really painful. You're only in Xi'an, you don't know the pain of having no water. If you were to go a few hundred miles west like me, you wouldn't even think about changing your palate by coming to the Northwest. Li Shilian said: I want to ask you, why are you going west? Jia Duocai laughed: That's going among the people. As he said this, the shop assistant brought the wine pot, cups, chopsticks, and a large plate of cold cuts. (26)

Dishevelled Hair and Left-Laid Lapel 223

— Yan Qiao

It's not that I'm old-fashioned and criticizing modern people, but the scenery before my eyes coincides so cleverly with what was said in ancient times that I can't help but bring it up for everyone to smile at. You must know that I am only doing archeology and not showing off my learning.

The Analects says (If it weren't for Guan Zhong, we would all have dishevelled hair and left-laid lapels!) Dishevelled hair and left-laid lapels were the appearance of barbarians at that time, who knew that after more than two thousand years, they would be called the epitome of modern fashion. Look, don't modern women have their hair scattered, all covering below the collar? According to Zhu Xi's interpretation, the word (被, bei), should be read as (披, pi), which is even more in line with the current fashion of short hair. As for the left-laid lapel, it doesn't seem to have been achieved yet, but according to Wang Renqiu's diary, the Qing Dynasty's jackets and mandarin jackets were left-laid lapel. He said:

(Left-laid lapel should be a double-breasted garment, opening in the middle, without the need for buttons, and a belt can be added. Barbarians can mount horses quickly, and when wrapping clothes, whether stretched or bent, they can also add knots and wraps, all left-laid lapel. The barbarians are also left-laid lapel. Today, the mandarin jackets in the Northwest have small lapels in the middle, with the right lapel covering the left, which is a joint creation.)

This explanation is more thorough than Zhu Xi's, so the Republic of China's formal dress, using mandarin jackets, has already used barbarians to transform the Chinese. Those who wear Western suits can use this point as a talisman.

However, Confucius's left-laid lapel must have referred to barbarian men. How is it that now these two things are distributed between men and women?

I remember during the Northern Expedition of the National Revolutionary Army, there was a rumor everywhere that they wanted to (overthrow the mandarin jacket,) and for a long time, mandarin jackets were not seen active in social circles. But now, when holding grand ceremonies, you can see long robes and short jackets jostling about. The other day at the Confucius ceremony in Qufu, no woman did not have dishevelled hair, and the men were all left-laid lapel. (Those who participated in the ceremony) don't know if Confucius saw it, would he sigh?

The New Life Movement prohibits women from perming their hair, but does not prohibit dishevelled hair. I think that looking like Wu Song on the stage is not only not beautiful, but also unclean. Although the Zhongshan suit is also evolved from Western suits, it is not left-laid lapel and is worth promoting. That wind collar button is not a genuine domestic product either, because before, they were all round collars or slanting lapels. So this account, I have to put aside and not talk about it.

Records of Fleeting Fragrance 224

— Original by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Now let me describe the details of these forty officials who came to the station to welcome the emperor: The first is the governor-general, Yuan Shikai, who has the power to command the armies of the entire Zhili province and Shandong and Henan provinces. Because he holds such strong power, he always stands in a leading position in name or in reality. Below him is the governor, who specializes in the civil administration of a province; the next is the treasurer (provincial treasurer), who is in charge of the province's finances: and then there is the judge (judicial commissioner) whose task is to specialize in hearing criminal cases within the province. Although these four are clearly designated to be in charge of the four different government affairs of the military, civil affairs, political law, and law, the boundaries of their powers and responsibilities are not clearly defined, and they can often interfere with or shirk each other's responsibilities. But these are beyond their control! In short, among these forty officials, these four can be regarded as the highest-ranking officials! Aside from them, the next in line would be the circuit intendants. At that time, each province was divided into several circuits, and each circuit had a presiding officer, which was called the circuit intendant. In terms of their official rank and status, they are similar to the mayors of today's special municipalities, but strictly speaking, they are completely different; because today's mayors often have direct contact with the people, the circuit intendants at that time absolutely disdained to consult on civil matters. They believed that the people were the most humble beings, and that if a high-ranking official were to directly contact the people, it would be a shameful thing. Therefore, they unloaded the responsibility of managing the people entirely on the state and county officials subordinate to them. Even if there were particularly diligent workers, they would only ask about a few of the more important matters.

Within Zhili Province, there were also seven officials of equal rank to the circuit intendant. Although there were seven of them, their tasks were very simple, generally just managing the small matter of minting silver coins, collectively known as the general managers of the mint. And this is not to say that they have any special research or experience in minting silver coins, so they are invited to guide or supervise them, but only because they want to be officials, their fathers, brothers, or relatives taught them to casually play a role.

Among these officials, there were two even more special ones, one called the Monk Registrar, and the other called the Taoist Registrar. Their positions were also equal to the circuit intendant; but their tasks were similar to those of foreign bishops. All they managed were temples and monks and Taoists. (136)

Snippets 225

— (Miao Shen)

Giving up a seat on the streetcar is originally a foreign custom. In principle, it is also a kind of courtesy from men to women; but when you see a woman carrying a lot of things, or holding a child on the streetcar, and you stand up to offer her a seat, but the woman doesn't even say thank you, but seems to accept it as a matter of course and sits down silently, where is the woman's courtesy then?

Deceitful Recruitment 226

— Drunken Fool

There are really many swindlers in Shanghai now, and the swindling techniques are becoming more and more strange. If you are a little careless, you will fall for their tricks. Even if you don't leave your house, someone will come to visit. They think of ways to extract money from your pocket. In particular, residents with (For Rent) signs are their target, and you must pay extra attention. The following is a true account of a neighbor's, the × family, being swindled!

The × family recently had a spare room for rent, so they put up a (For Rent) sign on the door. Early in the morning the other day, two neatly dressed men, A and B, came to see the room. They seemed very pleased with it, and the monthly rent was also agreed upon. According to the custom, a deposit of three dollars had to be paid first, and A took out a ten-dollar bill from the ×× bank to ask for change. The × family host looked at it again and again, saying it was good, and gave him seven dollars in change. Just as the two were about to leave, A pointed and said: A wooden stove should be arranged next to the terrace, and a pair of couches should be placed next to the railing. At this point, the second landlord did not agree. After arguing with the two for a long time, they finally broke up and returned the bill. A held it in his hand, about to return the seven dollars. B suddenly advised from the side, saying: We are very pleased with this house, it is a pity to abandon it. Why don't we accommodate it, we will find another way for those things. At this time, the second landlord was a little reluctant, and seeing them soften, he said it was very good. So the bill in A's hand was handed over again, and the date of moving in was explained, and the two of them left. The host looked at the bill again and found that it had become a fake bill. It turned out that in a moment of transfer, the real one had been switched. Realizing this, he sent someone to chase after them, but the two had already flown away like wild geese, their whereabouts unknown.

The second landlady ran out and said hatefully to the For Rent sign: I posted a For Rent sign, but I called in two swindlers, what real bad luck. After saying that, she tore the For Rent sign into pieces that flew away like butterflies.

To Mr. Shi Ji of Ningbo, The Novel Monthly we are collecting, Volume 22, is from issue number one to issue number five. We received one copy each of issue number one and issue number five. We are still missing issue numbers two, three, and four, a total of three copies. Please send us the supplements again. Sincerely, The Spring and Autumn Editorial Department.

Student Trilogy Part One (Elementary School Days) At the Beginning of Man, Nature is Good 227

Miscellaneous Talk

Thoughts on Japanese-Manchurian Enterprises (Part 1) 228

— Tianxu Wosheng

Reading the section (Investigation of Japanese Intrusion into Newly Established Enterprises in Northern Manchuria) published in the September 16th issue of Shen Bao, it mentions the first type of enterprise, namely the No. 1 and No. 2 flour mills, working day and night, producing as many as 3,200 bags per day, still thinking it is not enough, and in June of this year, the No. 3 plant was combined in Suihua, and on July 24, it began operating, producing 1,500 bags of flour per day, which can be said to be the ultimate prosperity. But its capital is only 2 million yuan. Since the Mitsui and Mitsubishi business groups are the investment center, and there are shares from the Japanese-established flour milling company and funds from the pseudo-Central Bank: it is of course easy to set it up immediately, which is not surprising. The flour milling industry, like our country's flour mills, absorbs agricultural products for large-scale production, which can make people use their talents and the land yield its resources. Our country has always valued agriculture and industry, and many flour mills have already been established. However, the raw materials they need, domestically produced ones are often too small in quantity and too high in price, so they take the convenience of foreign ones being cheaper, and choose to use them, and agricultural crops become more and more passive. A major crux of this is that tariffs have lost their control. If imported rice and wheat were taxed like alcohol, the tax rate would be equal to the selling price of locally produced liquor, it would of course be possible to avoid the adulteration of fire liquor with water to avoid the disadvantages of local liquor, and there would also be the possibility of self-producing alcohol in the country, because the raw materials for alcohol are also agricultural products. In addition to flour milling, the Japanese also set up an alcohol factory in Harbin with a capital of 1.67 million yuan, with the aim of using the abundant sorghum and saying that they are studying other crops, then rice wine, wheat wine, and sweet potatoes, grains, sugar cane, etc., will inevitably be readily available. This is the same as my proposed (Four People Relief Company) plan. If we want our country to be rich and strong, we must first value agriculture, and ensure that the income from farming can avoid hunger and cold, and avoid being hungry, so that they will not abandon their fields and flock to the cities, so that the vast fields will be desolate! Only when prices fluctuate, working hard all year round, and yet not being able to be full and warm, and even water and drought disasters come together, they abandon their plows and take risks, which is also a matter of urgency. Since silk is worthless, cutting down mulberry trees to plant other crops has also become a trend, just like a leaky boat in a big storm, crying to the sky, the disaster of sinking is just around the corner. In my opinion, there is only one way to save us from danger, that is, the captain should order us to quickly combine our efforts to plug the leak, so that foreign water cannot flood in in large quantities, and also order the boatmen to work desperately to accelerate the rate, and hope to reach the other shore. At this time of plugging the leak, any sacrifice will be spared. Rather than everyone on the same boat being submerged, it is better to sacrifice everything and fight with death, because this boat is just leaking, and has not yet reached the point of complete rupture. If we do not panic and abandon our sails and oars and cry like Chu people, there is still a way to remedy the situation. The so-called sails and oars are like plows. Now abandoning plows and seeking machinery is like trying to change a leaky boat into a steamship to increase speed. Even if there is a possibility of really changing it into a steamship in an instant, the sailors can immediately lose their jobs and stand idly by. However, the leak is not plugged, and it is already certain that its success will lead to the same demise. Therefore, I believe that the strategy for saving the country is to quickly plug the leak, and use tariffs as a barrier, which is just like the Yellow River's water control. On the one hand, we must build strong dikes to avoid being washed away, and on the other hand, we must do our best in ditches, unblocking what has been blocked, and restoring what has been abandoned. Most of them have remnants of past achievements, but if two people are paired together, working together, and cutting one foot wide and one foot deep, then there are tens of millions of people working together in the ditches at the same time, drawing a picture of entering the river and pouring into the sea, its speed should be like marching, with four routes advancing troops, all heading in one direction, then guiding according to the situation, how can there be such an extremely opposite scene of drought here and floods there? After Yu leveled the water and soil, the Yellow River disaster has not stopped in China, precisely because after Yu's death, no one continued his work, and they specialized in enjoying the fruits, not knowing how to improve, and filling rivers to make land, reversing the predecessors' achievements as foolish, not only Gun alone. Just like after Hou Ji taught the people how to farm, everyone eats ready-made food, and among the four classes, the scholars rank first, not farming and eating, not weaving and wearing, everyone wants to be a scholar, and their children do not want to keep their industry for generations, and they all tend to the path of not working and getting results. If one acre of land has one less person farming it, its output will decrease and consumers will increase, the demand exceeds the supply, and prices will naturally rise. Those who do not farm or weave cannot but eat and wear, then measuring expenses to make income, they must seek their livelihood, so they sell foreign goods, to reap the fisherman's profit, and make foreigners and our people the protagonists of the snipe and clam conflict, which is what Mencius called a mean man.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talking

Life and Survival 229

— Ze Cheng

What is so-called "life" (Live) is a rare thing in the world; most people are merely surviving, but is simply surviving enough?

The 19th-century English writer Oscar Wilde explained the difference between "survival" and "life" very clearly. He said, "Most people are alive, and starvation is rare; however, simply living such an ordinary life is no different from the lives of birds and beasts. They have no conscious sense of what it means to 'live,' and cannot rightly be said to be enjoying the pleasures of 'life.'"

"Why do we grow up in this world after all?" Those who can answer this question simply are, in the end, a very small minority. Most people fall from their mother's womb into a dream; and they dream forever, even to the point of carrying their drowsy fantasies into the deep grave.

In this era of distress, the remaining forces of feudalism are constantly assailing the youth; the whip of life is cruelly lashing their backs; under the gray and hideous wings of the demon of money, they are forced to rashly step off the track of life and squeeze into the trap of survival.

What a terrible phenomenon!

We, as young people, if we are sensitive and perceptive, will certainly not mistakenly fall into the trap that dissolves our spirit and destroys our souls. However, when we step onto the path of life, we must still carefully observe: one path, relatively flat and leading to darkness, is the side road of survival; the other, rugged but with a glimmer of light, is the grand road of life.

I hope that we are not just objects existing in the world. Nor should we betray our conscience and sell our souls.

I hope that we can bravely and resolutely follow on the path of life, that great tide of history, which is flooding and preparing to destroy everything, forging a bloody path to life, and becoming extraordinary people.

I know that most numb people still survive like objects.

I know that some young people are still wandering on the side roads of life.

Returning Home 230

— Sha Fei

Sitting on the train, I regretted that I should not have made this trip. There was a time when I could say that I was living a train life, but now I get a headache as soon as I see the station. The reason is that I can't even explain it myself, or maybe I just don't need to take the train now.

The train was delayed by twenty minutes from the scheduled time. We don't have to ask for the reason. It is said that on the northern line, it is not uncommon for trains to be derailed for three to five days, and passengers don't find it strange. However, those who are on the train every day don't seem to notice this. In these twenty minutes, I wanted to get off the train several times, and the passengers in the car showed signs of anxiety when the bell rang.

The day is the day before the Mid-Autumn Festival. Many companions are carrying large packages and small items to go home. I secretly laugh to myself. I wanted to leave a week ago, but it happened to coincide with this joyous festival of family reunion. So I thought of my home, my home deep in the white clouds!

Counting the days, it has been a full eight years since I left my hometown and drifted alone outside. When the signs of autumn sales fluttered in the dreary wind and rain, I realized that my wandering life had increased by another year, which was the ×th anniversary of my departure from my hometown. My old mother, my wife, and my newborn child, who should be nine years old now, must be looking forward to my return day and night. I received a letter from my hometown earlier this year, saying that if I had enough travel expenses for the journey, I should go home once! After receiving this letter, I cried all night. I seemed to see my old mother leaning on the door with a wooden cane, her silvery white hair being blown by the southern wind, which made people think of a kind of discordant feeling; my wife, my child, maybe even if I go back, they won't recognize their husband and father!

Far away, far away, my home on the shores of the South!

The train howled and stopped at every pier. It carried many wanderers to the bosom of their loving mothers; to the bosom of their wives. I wanted to find a companion in this carriage who, like me, had a home but could not return. We would cry loudly to commemorate our Mid-Autumn Festival.

But the carriage was full of smiling faces. They were going home, to such a sweet home, with old mothers, wives, and children. I asked myself why I didn't go back? Don't I have enough money for a one-way ticket? I didn't answer, because the answer couldn't even satisfy myself, that I couldn't go back to that home.

"(Lifting my head, I gaze at the bright moon; lowering my head, I think of my hometown)." Which poet wrote such lines? I unintentionally recalled these two lines of poetry, and cursed the author of the poem. Angrily, I withdrew my gaze from reality and turned it to the corner of the carriage. I saw a child holding a big mooncake and asking his father to share it with him. Speaking of mooncakes, they are the most famous in my hometown. Now the Cantonese-style mooncakes on Nanjing Road are already on sale at reduced prices. Shanghai people seem to pay special attention to eating. They like to eat local specialties. In fact, after eating the mooncakes from our hometown, these Shanghai "Cantonese-style" mooncakes are no longer authentic. Mooncakes are a common food in my hometown, but in this big city, they are used to decorate the good times and festivals. What's the reason for eating mooncakes during the Mid-Autumn Festival? Can the reunion fill the void in my heart?

The train passed through many piers, and the passengers in the carriage gradually thinned out. I hoped that when I reached the end point, I would be the only one left. So I picked up my worn-out suitcase, stepped off the train with the appearance of returning home, and stepped onto the station platform. Who knows that my home is on the distant shores of the South?

— Hong

Farmer: "I want to go to the city!"

City dweller: "I want to go to the countryside!"

The Secret Method for Obtaining Airplane Tickets 231

— Jing Yun

One day, I read such an advertisement in the newspaper: "Airplane tickets for this period can still be publicly researched, implemented according to law, and guaranteed to win. Regardless of whether you have already purchased them or not, or if you have purchased tickets multiple times without winning, please cut out this advertisement and send it by registered mail. All tests are free (the tests may be free, but the registration fee is naturally not 丨丨Yun's own note). After winning, a reward will be taken. Insurance can also be provided for horse racing to win exclusively, as well as all savings lottery tickets, guaranteed grand prizes, etc., all can be tried..."

Someone said: "The minds of Chinese people are very foolish, so many scientific inventions have to be left to foreigners." But how can it be like this? I think the minds of Chinese people are intelligent, clever, and transcendent. As long as you open your eyes and look at the advertisement for "The Secret Method for Obtaining Airplane Tickets," you can know that the airplane lottery tickets have only been opened for seven periods, and someone has actually researched the "secret method" to "guarantee winning." Compared with the "Airplane Lottery Ticket Purchase Method" published by a certain bookstore, this kind of clever intelligence, I am afraid that the foreign devils who invented science will also be stunned when they hear about it. However, the clever minds of Chinese people have never been willing to easily use it in science, but are willing to focus on this kind of thing. I remember that I used to meet a certain professor in a long black and blue cloth gown at the Jai Alai stadium every night, gambling until his face was red and his ears were hot. It is said that he was also researching the gambling method of Jai Alai. Unfortunately, this book has not been published until now. Otherwise, it could be compared with ("Airplane Secret Method") and ("With Secret Method") to form a triumvirate, benefiting the people!

The secret-keeping mentality of Chinese people is originally very strong. It is said that many good prescriptions of Bian Que and Hua Tuo, and many amazing boxing skills of the Shaolin Temple, were lost because they were kept too secret. Nowadays, many generations of famous doctors do not keep their ancestral prescriptions as if they were treasures, for fear of being discovered. Then, the inventor of this "Airplane Lottery Ticket Purchase Method" and the researcher of "The Secret Method for Obtaining Airplane Tickets," since he has researched the "guaranteed winning" method himself, wouldn't he go buy the tickets himself? Is he not afraid that other people will compete with him for the first prize of 500,000? I really don't quite understand whether they have really seen through the vulgarity and (regard wealth and nobility as floating clouds), don't want to become rich themselves, but are willing to travel around and calculate horoscopes for others for life?

This is just like the feng shui master who runs around in the mountains all day long, year after year, looking for good burial spots for people, and says to the landlord with oily mouth and slick tongue: "This dragon burial spot is so beautiful, burying it will guarantee wealth and glory." If it is really as he says, why doesn't he bury the bodies of his parents in there, so that he can go (wealth and glory) himself? The same question arises.

In this way, the secret method for obtaining airplane tickets can only be laughed at.

Women and Walking Sticks 232

— Jia

Oh, the walking stick women! As soon as I see every man on the street with a woman's arm hooked on his arm, with the same posture as hanging a walking stick, I can't help but shout in my heart.

Wherever I go, I have never seen a woman not hanging on a man's arm, tightly缠住 as if rooted, like ivy纏住 the wall. If she leaves even a little, she will not be able to stand steadily and will fall to the side. Therefore, she cannot leave the man's arm all day long, and always needs the man to hook her arm. When she leaves, she will be uneasy, feel lonely, and feel like a walking stick abandoned by its owner, lonely for no reason.

Women's walking sticks! In movie theaters and dance halls, women are even more like walking sticks, and they must have a man holding their arm as a guarantee. Then they laugh嘻嘻, as if to say, "I have a protector, I have an owner."

Walking sticks are inanimate, but women are animate and have a walking stick feeling. Hanging an inanimate walking stick is naturally more real than hanging a woman with an animate walking stick feeling, but the effect given to the person who is hanging is the same as the effect of a walking stick.

However, wandering loners prefer walking sticks without reality, and sometimes see them as more intimate than women with a walking stick feeling. This is because they are light and easy to carry on the street. They are not tiring at all, while women have the tiredness that walking sticks do not have. Moreover, women with a walking stick feeling are alive, they will be capricious and gluttonous. They want to eat German food in the morning and buy expensive cosmetics in the afternoon. If something goes wrong, they will hang on someone else's arm. Therefore, hanging on a woman with a walking stick feeling is time-sensitive with material ups and downs, so it is better to hang on a real walking stick, which is comfortable, without danger, and without worrying about its resistance.

There is a reason why loners prefer inanimate walking sticks and despise animate walking sticks.

An Undeliverable Letter 233

— Wan Song

Bing! As I pick up my pen to write this letter, my heart is filled with boiling blood! My hands are shaking! In my deep-set eye sockets, full of bloody tears, they are about to flow down with the tip of my pen!

As I write this letter, am I still in this dead society? Or have I already sacrificed myself for the masses? This is a mystery that has not been solved since we parted more than two years ago.

Some people say: After you left your hometown, when you went to ×Port, you bravely sacrificed yourself for the nation under the enemy's planes and artillery. Others say: In ×Port in × month of that year, I still saw your face and talked to you once. At that time, you were still full of energy doing your _____. According to him, you didn't encounter any accidents! But; you still don't know about my news, and it's the same as I don't know about your news! Then, even though we are in the same world, isn't it like being separated by a world?

Moreover, this society is already like it's dead, and there is nothing worth cherishing. Before the entire society is resuscitated, there is no difference between life and death, and reunion and separation are even more out of the question!

Mei died in the third month after you left. If you are not in the human world, but in another world, I think she might be able to find you and meet you? Otherwise, maybe she will leave me with a nightmare.

Li, and Xue, I used to raise them. When they grow up, I will _____, tell them _____, call them to follow your ambitions.

Mountain 234

— Ding Xing

There are no mountains here; where did the mountains go?

(The mountain was submerged in silver-white waves, and the turbulent waves sent it to the other side of the sea).

The mountain that accompanied our first love is not here!

I told Bing, who was on the other side of the sea, this sad news; then she comforted me and said:

It's good that there are no mountains, this can reduce the stimulation of your bitter memories, right?

However, although the shape of the mountain can no longer be found in this city; the memory it left in my lonely heart has not been blurred. Whenever the setting sun sinks in the west and the wilderness is vast, I wander alone on the grass. I painfully dream a daytime dream: I dream of the green mountain, and our green first love.

It's just a matter of this year, one early spring afternoon, Xiao Qiu first imprinted our footprints. At that time, the mountain was covered with a layer of light green, faint, the same color as the clothes Bing was wearing, reflecting each other. Thus, this green became the symbol of our first love.

However, a few months passed so briefly, and everything disappeared with it! The mountain had not yet begun to fade its green; and the joy of our reunion was replaced by the sorrow of a distant departure! And she? Now even the last attachment that the mountain gave us has become a painful memory of illusion:

It was a mid-summer evening, and we were sitting on the top of Xiao Qiu as usual; the strong smell of green grass all around coldly penetrated into our nostrils, and a lost mood, like an insect, crawled up and down in our hearts.

Bing held my hand that I had reached out to her, raised her head and looked up at a few light red floating clouds, and said slowly, heavily:

Go, Xing! For the future.

I stared at her face facing the sky from the side, and some fluid was moving on the surface of her eyes. I felt a sour hardness in my teeth, so I also raised my head and silently looked at the gray sky.

The evening tide wind blew from the opposite bay, and my heart was as vague and ethereal as the wind!

It's getting dark: the light red of the floating clouds turned gray.

Let's go back, it's getting late.

I shook Bing's stiff body and stood up wordlessly. From the top of Xiao Qiu, taking slow steps, along the small road that had imprinted thousands of our footprints, when we returned to the foot of the mountain. Bing looked back at the Xiao Qiu protruding in the vast atmosphere, slumped on my shoulder, unable to hold back the depression and sadness, sobbing and saying:

Xiao Qiu after this······?

Now, there are no mountains here: where did the mountains go?

(The turbulent waves sent the mountain to the other side of the sea.)

Autumn Heart 235

— Superman

After a few days of drizzle, autumn slipped across the treetops.

The wind of September brings the cool smell of autumn, white clouds wander in the pale blue sky, and the cicadas sing their unfallen funeral song in a desolate voice. The coolness has begun to fill the world, and the phoenix leaves are fluttering one by one, and the flame-like summer has melted away.

A kind of intoxication scattered on the ripe grape trellis warmly permeates the air and dominates people's souls: but the withered bitter lotus and the grass about to turn yellow by the pond weave a layer of thin new sorrow.

Autumn is here again, ah, the heart of the wanderer!

In the city, autumn also puts on her conscious veil.

The ladies are trying on newly made fashions, and the silk stocking shops may have increased some business; although there are still people trying cold drinks occasionally, the warm lily soup is ultimately welcomed by the times; the autumn sun softly dyes the platform where potted flowers are placed, men think of the maple leaves outside the city, and slaves are busy wiping the new guns bought by their masters.

The autumn moon surges out with crystal clear plain color,泻 on the treetops on the sidewalk on the street, leaking sparse broken shadows, the houses on both sides, one by one, close their shutters, and some reveal silk-like lights, and the lovers in the lights snuggled together especially tightly.

What is left on the street is only silence and desolation, the wind blows through the dark night, rolling up dead leaves and dust, and how many homeless wanderers are dotted in the wind and dew.

The consciousness of autumn is spinning on the felt hats of gentlemen, and wanderers think of the clothes kept in the usury shops.

Autumn is here again, ah, the heart of the wanderer!

The roar of machinery is rumbling on the edge of the earth, where there is no day and night, no health, health is rolled away by wheels and belts, and suffocating air constantly falls on the hair, they do not know what autumn is, steel and coal smoke replace the entire life, and each of them is deeply etched with forehead wrinkles by the hellish life.

For many years, there have been no ripe fields, and the land is full of desolation. Man-made disasters and natural disasters have swept through time and time again, and wars have ravaged repeatedly. The proper field tax has been levied for decades to come. The great foreign forces are indirectly and deeply invading. The farmers are ultimately left with nothing. The only property they have left, their bodies, are also getting lighter and lighter every day. Autumn loses her lyrical function for this hungry and cold group, and the autumn wind and autumn rain bring them death. They are waiting to die, and some are taking separate paths.

Amateur Mailbox

This column will answer readers' letters individually, select the main points for publication, and welcome readers to express their opinions on various issues. The editor will select and record them in this column to fulfill the responsibility of criticizing society and to serve as the mouthpiece of the public. However, please note the following points when submitting letters: (1) The author is responsible for the content; (2) The issue must be related to the public's knowledge and must not tend to be specialized; (3) Please indicate your real name and address (this column can keep secrets), and the pen name will be determined by the submitter when publishing; (4) The editor has the right to delete and modify the submissions, and those who attack individuals or are close to flattery will not be published; (5) Regardless of whether the submissions are published or not, they will not be returned; (6) No remuneration will be given.

Another Opinion on Going to the Northwest 236

Dear Editor:

The September 18th issue published Mr. Zhou Wei Zhi's (The Prerequisites for Going to the Northwest). First (how do you go), second (how do you live after you go). In my opinion, these two questions do not seem to be prerequisites. The prerequisite is why the slogan (going to the Northwest) was generated. Because of the bankruptcy of the countryside and the decline of various industries in the city, tens of thousands of unemployed people were created. But will the countryside go bankrupt for no reason? Will the city decline for no reason? No, this is entirely due to the economic invasion of imperialism, the chaos of domestic politics, and other natural and man-made disasters; generally, young people think that there is no way out under such circumstances, and they can only go to the border areas to find another way out, so the slogan (going to the Northwest) was generated. But I think it is not only difficult for young people to find a way out there, but also fundamentally wrong. For example, if you can get there, can you guarantee that the rural Northwest will not go bankrupt? Will the various industries in the city not decline? No one can guarantee this. Because under the trend of the powers' economic invasion and division of China, China's economic lifeline is completely in their hands. Since the cities and rural areas in the mainland of China have been created by them in such a situation, then won't the border areas also be the same as the mainland, and also go bankrupt and decline?

I think that in the current environment, going to the Northwest is like a fire in your own house, escaping to the neighbor's house, without wanting to put it out, and without wanting to go back to your own house to get anything. You just run to the neighbor's house, without thinking that if the fire is not put out, it will slowly spread over. Therefore, young people thinking of going to the Northwest to make a living can be said to be fearing difficulties and seeking temporary safety, and avoiding the responsibilities they should bear. I think young people should take responsibility and find ways to eliminate this terrible flame that can spread: how to prevent the countryside from going bankrupt? How to prevent various industries from declining and reducing unemployment? These are our prerequisites. Then you can reconsider the conditions that Mr. Zhou said (how do you go) and (how do you live after you go), and find ways to go to the Northwest.

Li Jun September 21st

Editor's Note: Since we published Mr. Zhou Weizhi's article (The Prerequisites for Going to the Northwest), we have received letters from several readers discussing it, which shows everyone's enthusiasm for studying realistic issues. The editor has decided to publish these letters one after another for the public to explore.

Novel

Uncle's Braid (16) 237

— Ling He

Ming bone world? What is the Ming bone world? This is something everyone doesn't understand. However, after the restoration, there was a revolution, and after the revolution, braids had to be cut. Sixth Grandpa understood this very well, so he couldn't help but touch his own small white braid, and couldn't help but say with some worry:

Third Master, I heard that in today's Ming bone world, braids must be cut, is that right?

Of course, look, I don't have a braid. Civilized people don't have braids.

Third Master had been to a foreign school after all, so he was a famous person, so he had to cut his braid. But First Master was also very famous, who doesn't know about Mr. Xu Zhai in our Big Field Stomach? Why does he still keep his braid? But maybe it's because he hasn't had a revolution yet? Sixth Grandpa secretly thought: He wasn't a famous person, so he could always keep this white braid and take it to the coffin. So he was very happy, and he said loudly:

Then we're all okay, we're not famous people!

Hearing what Sixth Grandpa said, everyone felt it made a lot of sense, and couldn't help but feel much relieved. Only Oldest Mao didn't think so. He thought that although he had never been famous, it would be good to cut his braid, at least when grinding tofu in the morning, his hair wouldn't be soaked in sweat, but he still didn't want to cut it off, he said:

Who wouldn't like to cut off their braid, but now we don't know whose world it is. If we cut it off now, and the Ming bone world doesn't become successful, and it becomes Emperor Xuantong's world again, then that would be terrible. Cutting off your braid is like killing your head.

Speaking of this, he felt his wife touch his back, so he immediately realized that he had said the wrong thing; hadn't Third Master cut his braid? So he quickly said back:

But of course Third Master knows we're different, you've been to a foreign school, you've seen more of the world than us, you wouldn't be wrong to do anything······

Of course, the foreigner began to speak: You live in the countryside all year round, so you naturally don't know what's happening outside. This time the revolutionaries are rising up, you have to know that it's to destroy the Qing Dynasty and transform it into the Republic. The Republic means no emperor, transforming into a people's country. In the past, it was an autocratic country, now it's a democratic country, so it's called the Republic. The Republic requires cutting off braids. As for saying that we can't determine which side's world it is now, then the Qing Dynasty is definitely doomed. Now which province isn't responding to the revolutionaries? The Qing Dynasty is only relying on Yuan Shikai, but Yuan Shikai is advocating negotiating peace with the revolutionaries. So you see, what can the Qing Dynasty do?
